<span id="freeTextContainer17449244507333443467">Not far from the city there is an ancient wood, forgotten by the modern world, where Mystery walks in the moonlight. He wears the shape of a stag, or a goat, or a horned man wearing a cloak of leaves. He is summoned by the music of the pipes or a fire of bones on Midsummer's Evening. He is chased by the hunt and shadowed by the wild girl.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6440110116440000885">I enjoyed it overall but I did not expect it to be practically half mafia story, half deep woodland story as the book cover and info on the back does not hint at the mafia involvement whatsoever. If I had picked the book up in a shop I may have read the first couple of pages and been put off by the beginning mafia scenes and not purchased it so I am glad I bought it offline and was not put off when I persevered with it thinking it was probably just setting a scene and the woodland scenes would s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6440110116440000885">I enjoyed it overall but I did not expect it to be practically half mafia story, half deep woodland story as the book cover and info on the back does not hint at the mafia involvement whatsoever. If I had picked the book up in a shop I may have read the first couple of pages and been put off by the beginning mafia scenes and not purchased it so I am glad I bought it offline and was not put off when I persevered with it thinking it was probably just setting a scene and the woodland scenes would soon occur, which is portrayed by the beautiful cover (which thankfully happens) . That said it worked well and it even got my pulse racing in some scenes, I came to enjoy the mafia scenes. The chapters involving Ali and Mally were the highlights for me as was any mention of what they call in this book greenmantle, also know as the greenman/cernunnos/pan etc. :)<br /><br />Some lines I remember from the book I enjoyed reading are:<br /><br />‘All roads lead to the same end. So it’s not so much which road you take, as how you take it.’ <br />‘Some things can’t be explained, some shouldn’t be and some lose their heart when they are.’ <br />‘It wasn’t the magic of the mystery that was important or the finding of it, but the quest itself.’ <br />‘He has always been a reflection of what one brings to him.’ <br />‘It’s important to know what a person was, but it’s more important to know what they are now.’ <br />‘Talking is not everything Ali, sometimes just being together is enough.’<br /><br />“Thank God, you’re okay,” she murmured into Ali’s ear. <br />“Let’s thank ourselves,” Ali said. “We’re the ones that did it.”<br /><br />AND I need to make a cloak like this one, it sounds lovely: ‘She could see that the cloak now appeared to be made of hundreds of pieces of cloth in the shapes of leaves, all sewn together.’<br /><br />I would like to read some more stories by Charles De Lint in the future <br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_367927043">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/367927043" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7381871-allyson" class="left imgcol" title="Allyson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442952804p2/7381871.jpg" alt="Allyson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/367927043?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 14, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7381871-allyson" class="user" title="Allyson">Allyson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer367927043">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13004623915703431634">This is the second book by Charles de Lint that I've read, and I'm totally hooked. The story was not at all what I expected, in the best possible way. How many fantasy novels have you read that started off depicting the aftermath of a mafia hit? I'm guessing none. And yet de Lint is such a masterful storyteller that he manages to weave together the backgrounds and needs of a wide variety of characters without ever letting the reader feel confused, lost, or disinterested. Before long, it's making</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13004623915703431634">This is the second book by Charles de Lint that I've read, and I'm totally hooked. The story was not at all what I expected, in the best possible way. How many fantasy novels have you read that started off depicting the aftermath of a mafia hit? I'm guessing none. And yet de Lint is such a masterful storyteller that he manages to weave together the backgrounds and needs of a wide variety of characters without ever letting the reader feel confused, lost, or disinterested. Before long, it's making perfect sense that our protagonists include a retired mafia hit man, a recent lottery winner, and a little girl. It makes perfect sense that we also learn about the inhabitants of a hidden village, a mysterious entity that may or may not be a god, a small time thug who wants to be much bigger than his britches can handle, a random local guy who's just in the wrong place at the wrong time, and a forest "secret" that sometimes seems like a raggamuffin girl and sometimes like an ancient faerie.<br /><br />Besides the technical prowess, I think what I enjoyed most about this story was that, despite the elements of fantasy, it could just as easily been categorized as mainstream fiction. Sort of how Stephen King started off as horror but became so popular he transcended the genre. Like King, de Lint blurs the edges of the real world to show us a possibility that might exist right under our noses. However, his writing is also extraordinary, literary and lyric, authentic and easy.<br /><br />This was so enjoyable, I got depressed when I finished it! I can't wait to read more of de Lint's work.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13004623915703431634">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_311937298">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311937298" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5208457-d-m-dutcher" class="left imgcol" title="D.M. Dutcher "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1338694848p2/5208457.jpg" alt="D.M. Dutcher " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/311937298?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 13, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5208457-d-m-dutcher" class="user" title="D.M. Dutcher ">D.M. Dutcher </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5208457-d-m-dutcher?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5208457-d-m-dutcher?shelf=overrated" class="actionLinkLite">overrated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer311937298">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14114361159467410552">Meh. A bunch of different characters like a former mafia hitman, a divorced wife and her bright daughter, a bunch of neopagan villagers, and a mysterious wild girl all live in the wilds of Canada. They all are touched by a gigantic stag as the past of several of them come to a violent head.<br /><br />It starts out well, but then drags on. I'm sure for the time the neo-paganism was groundbreaking, but it feels really tired and cliche here, especially the typical "Christianity is bad m'kay" vibe. I'm not aga</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14114361159467410552">Meh. A bunch of different characters like a former mafia hitman, a divorced wife and her bright daughter, a bunch of neopagan villagers, and a mysterious wild girl all live in the wilds of Canada. They all are touched by a gigantic stag as the past of several of them come to a violent head.<br /><br />It starts out well, but then drags on. I'm sure for the time the neo-paganism was groundbreaking, but it feels really tired and cliche here, especially the typical "Christianity is bad m'kay" vibe. I'm not against the idea of functioning paganism in fantasy, but a good book doesn't greenwash it: it acknowledges that the deity itself is not perfect. A good example in modern film is Miyazaki's Princess Mononoke, with the wolf-goddess Moro. She is wild, pagan, capricious, but tender and long-lived. This just felt very one-sided a book to me, especially when they revealed the dogs chasing the stag.<br /><br />The plot is okay, but after awhile I was just wishing they'd get to the resolution. The pagan aspect was straightforwards and displayed early, so it's just a lot of waiting for Earl vs Tony or what have you. Surprisingly I found myself differing from the reviewers here, and I would have loved it just being a story about Tony, Frankie, and Ali discovering a wild pagan god in their forest. The rest of the characters or subplots honestly felt redundant, and those characters to me were the only ones that mattered. The neopagan village especially was a dumb idea, as it robbed a lot of the mystery of the book. I'll still try later books, but this one isn't really selling me on the author.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14114361159467410552">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/4789256-lilia" class="left imgcol" title="Lilia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1294727606p2/4789256.jpg" alt="Lilia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/182384957?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 29, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4789256-lilia" class="user" title="Lilia">Lilia</a>

          added it




        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer182384957">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15958696585232451599">My opinion isn't objective, since I first laid my hands upon his books, but I will try my best anyway.<br /><br />This book took me longer to finish than others, something in the plot seemed more different than his usual "style" of writing. Maybe it's just because I don't like much action, guns and violence in my books, maybe he took a different path of storytelling. <br />Anyhow, no matter how much I was disappointed with the whole "Godfather" mess that he described here and gave less space for the magical line</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15958696585232451599">My opinion isn't objective, since I first laid my hands upon his books, but I will try my best anyway.<br /><br />This book took me longer to finish than others, something in the plot seemed more different than his usual "style" of writing. Maybe it's just because I don't like much action, guns and violence in my books, maybe he took a different path of storytelling. <br />Anyhow, no matter how much I was disappointed with the whole "Godfather" mess that he described here and gave less space for the magical line of events to develop, when I finished the last page I had the same feeling as I always do when I finish his books - the crave for more. <br /><br />I give it 3 out of 5, but nonetheless will continue searching, reading and collecting his books.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer193403530">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8172308741594386099">This was a magical and amazing book that transported me to a reality where the Horned One still roams the woods accompanied by various companions, both good and evil.<br /><br />This wondrous tale involves a single mother, her otherworldly teenage daughter and a former mob hitman living outside a small town in Canada where mystical creatures still roam.<br /><br />To throw some wrenches into the works are the mother's larcenous ex-husband and the hitman's former employer. How it all resolves is both gripping and awesom</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8172308741594386099">This was a magical and amazing book that transported me to a reality where the Horned One still roams the woods accompanied by various companions, both good and evil.<br /><br />This wondrous tale involves a single mother, her otherworldly teenage daughter and a former mob hitman living outside a small town in Canada where mystical creatures still roam.<br /><br />To throw some wrenches into the works are the mother's larcenous ex-husband and the hitman's former employer. How it all resolves is both gripping and awesome.<br /><br />This is the type of book that is rather hard to describe but once you start reading you are transported. When I finished, I felt as though I were emerging from a trip to another world still filled with mystery and magic.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1171329354">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1171329354" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7442439-brian-darvell" class="left imgcol" title="Brian Darvell"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Brian Darvell" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1171329354?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7442439-brian-darvell" class="user" title="Brian Darvell">Brian Darvell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1171329354">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10133736003586439260">I chose Greenmantle solely because I read that it was a good start to reading anything by de Lint. His style of Urban Fantasy is unique because it combines both the aspects of traditional fiction with aspects of fantasy. This undoubtedly gets many true Fantasy aficionados upset that his work should be considered Fantasy at all but I now tend to disagree with these beliefs since reading this novel.<br /><br />Greenmantle on the whole is just a simple, yet good, story. There's nothing in the way of true discu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10133736003586439260">I chose Greenmantle solely because I read that it was a good start to reading anything by de Lint. His style of Urban Fantasy is unique because it combines both the aspects of traditional fiction with aspects of fantasy. This undoubtedly gets many true Fantasy aficionados upset that his work should be considered Fantasy at all but I now tend to disagree with these beliefs since reading this novel.<br /><br />Greenmantle on the whole is just a simple, yet good, story. There's nothing in the way of true discussion upon society or politics. His development of friendship between adults and children was very good I thought and his style of writing is very peaceful and easy to follow. This novel is easily just as accessible for teenagers as it is for adults and I would recommend this novel to anyone looking for a good novel to read. It is especially adequate for those who dislike reading true Fantasy novels because of their inherent 'far out' nature but who still wish to read a novel with a bit of the mystic and mysterious.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10133736003586439260">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2504140-kristal?shelf=mythology" class="actionLinkLite">mythology</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1052881806">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16864857160607465970">Tony was a hitman in New York City before he was set up and a price was put on his head. Frankie and Ali are a mother and daughter team who are hoping that the money from a lotto win will help them finally settle down and restore Frankie's childhood home and they can live a normal life. By accident, the three meet and quickly discover that there are things living in the woods behind their Canadian home. Some things are friendly and want to help while other things are there to only cause hurt. To</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16864857160607465970">Tony was a hitman in New York City before he was set up and a price was put on his head. Frankie and Ali are a mother and daughter team who are hoping that the money from a lotto win will help them finally settle down and restore Frankie's childhood home and they can live a normal life. By accident, the three meet and quickly discover that there are things living in the woods behind their Canadian home. Some things are friendly and want to help while other things are there to only cause hurt. Together, the three must unite and each must learn how to defend themselves and stand up to the ones trying to hurt them. <br /><br />This was my first time to read Charles de Lint and I will definitely be picking up more by this author. I stick to my opinion that sometimes books mean more to a certain reader when they are read at the perfect time in one's life. And maybe that is what has happened to me with this book. For me, it also combined two of my favorite subjects - Italian Mafia and Folklore. I know those two things have nothing in common but de Lint manages to bring them together and create a fast-paced story full of mystical moments and mafia-madness. My only complaint would be that ending was rather rushed and not all the ends tied up neatly. But it had reached so high in the beginning, I am still a huge fan. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1016784732?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 04, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12154055-alex-long" class="user" title="Alex Long">Alex Long</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1016784732">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2284750519567832839">This is a fun novel that had excellent pacing. It reads like a television show, with viewpoints switching between characters just as their individual story has reached a sort of climax in order to evoke suspense for when their story picks back up again. <br />The things I didn't like about they book are explained by it being written a while ago when the elements in it weren't so overused. The main character is a fourteen year old girl who's a bookworm who longs for adventure and is brave...like every</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2284750519567832839">This is a fun novel that had excellent pacing. It reads like a television show, with viewpoints switching between characters just as their individual story has reached a sort of climax in order to evoke suspense for when their story picks back up again. <br />The things I didn't like about they book are explained by it being written a while ago when the elements in it weren't so overused. The main character is a fourteen year old girl who's a bookworm who longs for adventure and is brave...like every protagonist in every book about a child now. And it really hits you over the head with it's feminist message. The message itself that women should be independent of men and that there's no real significant difference aside from the physical makeup of their body is talked about, but then in the action the women in the novel are still damsels in distress while mafia people have cowboy shootouts around them. Once the 14 year old is rescued by a weird magic girl who keeps stealing people's shit, so there's that. And I liked the similarities displayed between Christ and Paganism, particularly the mystery religion about Pan, but to me its arguments didn't really seem that interesting because this was written 20 or so years ago when I think they were pretty new. And as a Christian I kind of felt weird that the main villains of the book were evil ghost monks who try to kill Pan(or greenmantle or whatever) and forcibly convert the teenage girl to their religion. But that's just my bias, it didn't really detract from the story itself, and the scene was really dramatic so I liked it. THanks Ms. Williams for recommending this author to me. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2284750519567832839">...more</a>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer326708775">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13600930093692528709">This novel's blend of urban fantasy elements with Italian mob intrigues was an unexpected, but clever, combination of opposites. Canadian folk-lore (remnants from British settlers) is a major element of the plot here, but it is overshadowed by the human concerns of the real world: a potential kidnapping for money and a crime-sydicate feud. Even though the focus was more on the urban than the fantasy elements, I still found this novel to be highly interesting because Charles touches on a theme th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13600930093692528709">This novel's blend of urban fantasy elements with Italian mob intrigues was an unexpected, but clever, combination of opposites. Canadian folk-lore (remnants from British settlers) is a major element of the plot here, but it is overshadowed by the human concerns of the real world: a potential kidnapping for money and a crime-sydicate feud. Even though the focus was more on the urban than the fantasy elements, I still found this novel to be highly interesting because Charles touches on a theme that is prevalent regardless of content. The primal Mystery of the world is never going to leave, no matter how industrialized things get, because no one can explain everything and some things are better left to being Secrets. We may have explained the "magic" in gunpowder with science, but it's still a spark that had to come from somewhere!<br /><br />Though I totally just realized that we never get to find out of the problems with the Don in New York ever get resolved! He may have gotten taken out, along with his sons, BUT that doesn't mean that Valenti's problems are all over!</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_379678582">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379678582" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6333844-dina" class="left imgcol" title="Dina"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1408988268p2/6333844.jpg" alt="Dina" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/379678582?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 02, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6333844-dina" class="user" title="Dina">Dina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2216225.Greenmantle" title="Paperback 9780441302956" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer379678582">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12240823004666458374">First encounter with de Lint. Picked this up at a great indie bookstore in Seattle (really, all indie bookstores there are great.) Recommendation from the owner when I stated a preference for fantasy that crosses world boundaries.<br /><br />Cultural refs are somewhat dated. Not sure I got all of them. De Lint has a habit of making not-so-subtle shout-outs to his fantasy author contemporaries and also name-drops a number of bigwigs in the neopagan movement (Crowley, Regardie, Buckland, etc.) that distracts.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12240823004666458374">First encounter with de Lint. Picked this up at a great indie bookstore in Seattle (really, all indie bookstores there are great.) Recommendation from the owner when I stated a preference for fantasy that crosses world boundaries.<br /><br />Cultural refs are somewhat dated. Not sure I got all of them. De Lint has a habit of making not-so-subtle shout-outs to his fantasy author contemporaries and also name-drops a number of bigwigs in the neopagan movement (Crowley, Regardie, Buckland, etc.) that distracts.<br /><br />Character clearly comes secondary to the story of ‘the Mystery’ (seeming more like simplistic archetypes), though it is interesting how the mythic element influences the modern day elements—where a number of disparate lives eventually intersect. At first I found myself thinking <em>‘Who the hell are all these people?’</em> The intersection occurs gradually; too gradually in fact, as there were times I found myself wishing de Lint would just get on with the impending confrontation and stop bread crumbing. Some plot elements also seemed like unnecessary detours—mostly the Mafia ones (yes- that Mafia), although I see why some of this was relevant as establishing background for Tony’s character arc. (I’m not a fan of Mafia stuff, so that might be weighting my opinion).<br /><br />Ali = girl hero<br />Tony = fallen warrior<br />Frankie = damsel in distress<br />Earl = nemesis<br />Greenmantle/Pan = god/divine/mythic aspect<br /><br />I most enjoyed the descriptions of encounters between modern and mysterious elements. De Lint has a genuine facility with detail and conveying the sense of wonder inherent in the collision of times and worlds. I also liked the ideas about mysteries and the concepts of bleed-through from one world to another, although some of these seem markedly slanted with anti-Christian rhetoric. Ended up sounding a little like pro-pagan proselytizing.<br /><br />Not a fast read; kept me turning pages, yet didn't really snag my devotion. Most interesting to find in an author's note in back from de Lint that a scene Kenneth Grahame's <a title="The Wind in the Willows by Kenneth Grahame" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5659.The_Wind_in_the_Willows">Wind in the Willows</a> partly inspired the story.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12240823004666458374">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6176152186130883045">Greenmantle (I think) is one of the better novels to come from de Lint. It is certainly a faster paced story and slightly less dreamy compared to his other works. I found it to me more 'real' and gritty which gave it an air of believability to it as well. It contains all the subtleties that have to do with the pagan influence that de Lint draws from while maintaining his well developed characters.<br /><br />A great read for anyone how is interested in exploring the fantastic worlds that are woven between o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6176152186130883045">Greenmantle (I think) is one of the better novels to come from de Lint. It is certainly a faster paced story and slightly less dreamy compared to his other works. I found it to me more 'real' and gritty which gave it an air of believability to it as well. It contains all the subtleties that have to do with the pagan influence that de Lint draws from while maintaining his well developed characters.<br /><br />A great read for anyone how is interested in exploring the fantastic worlds that are woven between our own as only de Lint cant present them.<br /><br /><br />Plot ***Spoilers***<br />Frankie Treasure wins the Wintario lottery, packs up her daughter, Alice ("Ali"), and moves into the home where she grew up, after renovating it, even though her deceased father made her childhood there miserable. Everything seems good, for a while. Unfortunately, Frankie's ex-husband, Earl, hears about Frankie's good fortune. Earl has developed into a first-class thug, with mob connections, and he decides that he can kidnap his daughter and get the lottery money from his ex-wife. Karl can then use it to finance a big-time drug deal. <br />Meanwhile, Tony Valenti, a fratellanza (Mafia) hit-man, ends up on the wrong side of an internal power struggle in his Family, and goes into hiding, one block away from the old/new home of Frankie and Ali Treasure. What none of them knows is that, not far away, back in the woods, there is a hidden village of people who reject the modern world and modern religions, in favor of a worship of nature and the Horned God of the Forest. </span>

      <a href="/user/show/9199006-barbara-gordon" class="user" title="Barbara Gordon">Barbara Gordon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer390338832">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18307342663443057599">Getting a late start on this, the book that seems to be de Lint's best known. Previously I'd read Mulengro, which I suppose isn't typical of his work, and the 'Jack' books, so I'm not exactly well-versed. I did feel that I should have read Dunsany's The Blessing of Pan, first, since de Lint says it was the springboard for his book.<br />I found some of the same problems as I did with Mulengro, in that the book feels lumpy. The low-life and criminal thread was better integrated into the main story than</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18307342663443057599">Getting a late start on this, the book that seems to be de Lint's best known. Previously I'd read Mulengro, which I suppose isn't typical of his work, and the 'Jack' books, so I'm not exactly well-versed. I did feel that I should have read Dunsany's The Blessing of Pan, first, since de Lint says it was the springboard for his book.<br />I found some of the same problems as I did with Mulengro, in that the book feels lumpy. The low-life and criminal thread was better integrated into the main story than it was in Mulengro, but the fantasy thread felt loose until the last, maybe, quarter of the book. I liked the characters of Ali (bookish girl) and Valenti (retired hitman), and their friendship worked well, but when the story moved to Lewis and the secret village of New Wolding everything slowed to a crawl. Maybe I just read too much Machen and Dunsany in my early years and this was too much like re-warmed porridge. Not that I don't like porridge, but it's better hot.<br /><br />ETA: Does anyone think the Lance thread added anything to the book at all? He's the guy who hears the music and ends up shooting his dog, Dooker. It reminded me of the undead thug thread in Mulengro, which read like an imitation of Robert McCammon when he was imitating Stephen King.<br />But I did like the Jack books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18307342663443057599">...more</a>

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer96983456">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1040287176650736314">I really enjoyed Greenmantle. My one complaint was that the author didn't do a good enough job establishing what was going on with the supernatural parts of the story. I liked the links with various mythologies, but I felt like the philosophical implications were kind of confusing. They seemed to be saying that humans created the Mystery with their beliefs, but also that the mystery couldn't be irreparably corrupted by them. <br />I liked the juxtaposition of the big city East Coast mafia set up with</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1040287176650736314">I really enjoyed Greenmantle. My one complaint was that the author didn't do a good enough job establishing what was going on with the supernatural parts of the story. I liked the links with various mythologies, but I felt like the philosophical implications were kind of confusing. They seemed to be saying that humans created the Mystery with their beliefs, but also that the mystery couldn't be irreparably corrupted by them. <br />I liked the juxtaposition of the big city East Coast mafia set up with the rural Canada/Celtic mythology setting. I also really liked how they described Greenmantle as being both the hunter and the prey and then the male lead, Tony, was also someone who had been both hunter and prey, and yet was noble. All in all, a good book, but not one of de Lint's best.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_204256422">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204256422" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4313474-cupcakencorset" class="left imgcol" title="Cupcakencorset"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1284983423p2/4313474.jpg" alt="Cupcakencorset" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/204256422?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 06, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4313474-cupcakencorset" class="user" title="Cupcakencorset">Cupcakencorset</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer204256422">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4714220122195348497">Written in 1988, this is the earliest of de Lint's books that I've read (I think) and it does a terrific job of introducing the magic and whimsy and mystery of the world he has created. This one is set in eastern Canada. It crosses the young-punk New York mob, old-school New York mob, the 14-year-old daughter and the former wife of a dirt-bag drug dealer with old-world mystery and secrets. The result is a surprising, dark, delightful, mystical intersection, with engaging characters and an innova</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4714220122195348497">Written in 1988, this is the earliest of de Lint's books that I've read (I think) and it does a terrific job of introducing the magic and whimsy and mystery of the world he has created. This one is set in eastern Canada. It crosses the young-punk New York mob, old-school New York mob, the 14-year-old daughter and the former wife of a dirt-bag drug dealer with old-world mystery and secrets. The result is a surprising, dark, delightful, mystical intersection, with engaging characters and an innovative take on myth-building that will serve as the basis for de Lint's other works. Highly recommended.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2686660445152056733">This book was quite captivating in that it reminded me of the childhood fantasies that I had about being transported into another fantasy realm, or discovering mythical creatures within our own world. I also very much liked de Lint's discussion of the role that myth and "mystery" play in our cultures and in our psyches. The characters somehow were not as compelling as I had hoped they would be. Most of the main bad guys, as well as one of the main heroes, were mafia members, and I've never been</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2686660445152056733">This book was quite captivating in that it reminded me of the childhood fantasies that I had about being transported into another fantasy realm, or discovering mythical creatures within our own world. I also very much liked de Lint's discussion of the role that myth and "mystery" play in our cultures and in our psyches. The characters somehow were not as compelling as I had hoped they would be. Most of the main bad guys, as well as one of the main heroes, were mafia members, and I've never been particularly enthralled with that culture, so that could have been part of the problem.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_344974595">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344974595" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-campbell" class="left imgcol" title="Nenia Campbell"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1435654700p2/2190064.jpg" alt="Nenia Campbell" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/344974595?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 06, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-campbell" class="user" title="Nenia Campbell">Nenia Campbell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer344974595">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2398604153115787438"><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380380229ra/737056.gif" /><br /><br />i mean, i <strong>could</strong> if i really to, but i don't want to. finish the book, that is. because the problem is that <em>greenmantle</em> is all over place. for example, this is a <strong>fantasy novel</strong> but it starts out like <a title="The Godfather by Mario Puzo" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22034.The_Godfather">the godfather</a> by <a title="Mario Puzo" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12605.Mario_Puzo">mario puzo</a>.<br /><br /><blockquote>by the time eddie "the squeeze" pinelli was five hours dead, valenti was on a boeing 747 halfway across the atlantic.</blockquote><br /><br />my first thought was, "did someone take the cover of a fantasy novel and swap it with one of those stupid sequels to the godfather?" i'm all for the element</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2398604153115787438"><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380380229ra/737056.gif" /><br /><br />i mean, i <strong>could</strong> if i really to, but i don't want to. finish the book, that is. because the problem is that <em>greenmantle</em> is all over place. for example, this is a <strong>fantasy novel</strong> but it starts out like <a title="The Godfather by Mario Puzo" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22034.The_Godfather">the godfather</a> by <a title="Mario Puzo" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12605.Mario_Puzo">mario puzo</a>.<br /><br /><blockquote>by the time eddie "the squeeze" pinelli was five hours dead, valenti was on a boeing 747 halfway across the atlantic.</blockquote><br /><br />my first thought was, "did someone take the cover of a fantasy novel and swap it with one of those stupid sequels to the godfather?" i'm all for the element of surprise, but when your plot is so vague it leaves the reader wondering if they're reading the right genre that's not really conducive to your purpose as a writer. you want suspense, not <strong>complete and utter confusion</strong>.<br /><br />if the book's cover didn't have a picture of a deer's head on a man's body, i would never even have guessed it was a fantasy novel. not with a beginning like that. and from the way the opening is totally vague about who valenti is and what his m.o. is all about, you might think that he's not a very important character. but no--valenti's one of our <strong>main characters</strong>.<br /><br />one of? that's right. there's moar! when valenti moves from new york to canada to escape some problems with his don, he meets our other main characters--a mother and daughter who are best friends forever!!!1<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380380229ra/737057.gif" /><br /><em>"my mom's totally number 1 in my top 8 on myspace! :)"</em><br /><br />their names are frankie and ali. frankie is one of those women who's childlike and totally gets mistaken as being her daughter's <strong>sister</strong> <em>all the time</em> because she's hot stuff. ali is so bored by her peers who <strong>just don't understand her</strong> and she takes refuge in fantasy novels--and we are battered again and again with lists of what constitutes ali's favorite reading material because it is quite obviously mr. de lint's favorite reading material, too, and those other authors probably paid him to endorse their books...<br /><br />and then there's this mysterious people living in the woods who come out and play music and sneak into the humans' houses to watch them sleep and sometimes steal borrow stuff and their music does "things" to people. and they like to watch as these "things" happen. why? it's not quite clear. the music does different things to different people; it kind of shows their true character (i.e. whether they're good or bad). but we never actually find out <strong>what</strong> these people are. faeries? elves? witches? pagans? a pervert colony?<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379768879i/272648.png" /><br /><em>"hurr durr i watch you sleep."</em><br /><br />oh and frankie's creepy ex-husband is after her because she just won a lottery and he wants to steal it. he's decided a good way to do this would be to kidnap their daughter and hold her hostage until she gets the money for him. and if frankie doesn't pay up, he'll kill ali--or torture her. it'll learn her some respect for her old man. also, he works with the mafia that is chasing down valenti. small world, huh?<br /><br /><img class="hostedImg escapedImg" style=";display:none;" src="http://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380380229r/737058.gif?v=1452558986059" /><img class="escapedImg loadingImg" src="/assets/loading-trans.gif" /><br /><em>"you gonna get raeped."</em><br /><br />but valenti just so happens to have uzis and semi-automatics in his house and he's like, "i will be your knight, fair damsels--particularly you, ms. milf, maam." and i could tell that valenti and frankie were going to hook up at some point in this novel. ugh. please, book, at least <strong>try</strong> to be subtle. please? for me?<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380380229ra/737059.gif" /><br /><em>"i may be a gangster, but i still have feels."</em><br /><br />ahhhhh!!!!! too many tropes!<br /><br />maybe this book would be right for some people, but i couldn't get into it. de lint tries too hard to be mysterious and the end result was that i had no idea what the flip was going on. showing and not telling is good, but sometimes you have to clue the reader in.<br /><br />so while this book is not going to be making any of my favorites lists any time soon i suppose for a situational comedy, it's not too ba--<br /><br />wait, what? what's that? you mean, this book is supposed to be <em>serious</em>? it's <strong>not</strong> supposed to be a comedy?<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380380229ra/737060.gif" /><br /><em>"LOL JK. never mind."</em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2398604153115787438">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_87929978">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87929978" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2362855-rick-piatt" class="left imgcol" title="Rick Piatt"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Rick Piatt" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/87929978?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 09, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2362855-rick-piatt" class="user" title="Rick Piatt">Rick Piatt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer87929978">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5566307289057441272">This was my first DeLint. It was unlike anything I'd read before and I sure enjoyed it. I typically read Fantasy or Epic Fantasy predominantly. But to tell the truth the idea of putting "fantasy creatures" here in the world where I live creeps me out completely. Every time I picked up the book it gave me that same feeling I had as a kid on Halloween going through a haunted house. I love it, I love it, I love it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N3hwh61fK+/Crryc0mhY+vfRKLZ9mMUiQva59H05cGhSrE9UX40/FU52yCesCb5IvibrrzRFgogo/7xmsayGLQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

How did the good father die&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText5334562636321285865\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;&amp;quot;Should I have taken the false teeth?&amp;quot; This is what Dr. Jonathan Hullah, a former police surgeon, thinks after he watches Father Hobbes die in front of the High Altar at Toronto\'s St. Aidan\'s on the morning of Good Friday. How did the good father die? We do not learn the answer until the last pages of this &amp;quot;Case Book&amp;quot; of a man\'s rich and highly observant life. But we learn much more about many things, and especially about Dr. Hullah. From an early age, Jonathan Hullah developed &amp;quot;a high degree of cunning&amp;quot; in concealing what his true nature might be. And so he kept himself on the outside, watching, noticing, and sniffing, most often in the company of those who bore watching. Among them, flamboyant, mystical curate Charlie Iredale; outrageous banker Darcy Dwyer; cynical, quixotic professor Brocky Gilmartin, whose son Conor, also Hullah\'s godson, makes a fateful and too brief appearance in Robertson Davies\'s last novel, Murther &amp;amp; Walking Spirits. Hullah also lives in close proximity to Pansy Freake Todhunter, an etcher in Toronto. Indeed he becomes privy to her intimate letters to British sculptor Barbara Hepworth. It is &amp;quot;Chips,&amp;quot; as she is called, who writes Dame Barbara: &amp;quot;The doctor is a bit of a puzzle. Long and cornery and quiet and looks like a horse with a secret sorrow.&amp;quot; As the Cunning Man takes us through his own long and ardent life of theatre, art, and music, varied adventures in the Canadian Army during World War II, and the secrets of a doctor\'s consulting room, his preoccupation is not with sorrow but with the comedic canvas of life. Just as Dr. Hullah practices a type of psychosomatic medicine &amp;quot;by which I attempt to bring about changes in the disease syndromes through language,&amp;quot; so does Robertson Davies intertwine language and story, as perhaps never before, to offer us profound truths about being human.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"5334562636321285865\" href=\"#\"     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8185168.Charles_de_Lint">About Charles  de Lint</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/8185168.Charles_de_Lint"><img alt="8185168" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1400347166p2/8185168.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer9923028872958170514">Charles de Lint is the much beloved author of more than seventy adult, young adult, and children's books. Renowned as one of the trailblazers of the modern fantasy genre, he is the recipient of the World Fantasy, Aurora, Sunburst, and White Pine awards, among others. Modern Library's Top 100 Books of the 20th Century poll, conducted by Random House and voted on by readers, put eight of de Lint's b</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9923028872958170514">Charles de Lint is the much beloved author of more than seventy adult, young adult, and children's books. Renowned as one of the trailblazers of the modern fantasy genre, he is the recipient of the World Fantasy, Aurora, Sunburst, and White Pine awards, among others. Modern Library's Top 100 Books of the 20th Century poll, conducted by Random House and voted on by readers, put eight of de Lint's books among the top 100.<br />De Lint is a poet, folklorist, artist, songwriter and performer. He has written critical essays, music reviews, opinion columns and entries to encyclopedias, and he's been the main book reviewer for The Magazine of Fantasy &amp; Science Fiction since 1987. De Lint served as Writer-in-residence for two public libraries in Ottawa and has taught creative writing workshops for adults and children in Canada and the United States. He's been a judge for several prominent awards, including the Nebula, World Fantasy, Theodore Sturgeon and Bram Stoker.<br /><br />Born in the Netherlands in 1951, de Lint immigrated to Canada with his family as an infant. The family moved often during de Lint's childhood because of his father's job with an international surveying company, but by the time Charles was twelve—having lived in Western Canada, Turkey and Lebanon—they had settled in Lucerne, Quebec, not far from where he now resides in Ottawa, Ontario.<br /><br />In 1980, de Lint married the love of his life, MaryAnn Harris, who works closely with him as his first editor, business manager and creative partner. They share their love and home with a cheery little dog named Johnny Cash.<br /><br />Charles de Lint is best described as a romantic: a believer in compassion, hope and human potential. His skilled portrayal of character and settings has earned him a loyal readership and glowing praise from peers, reviewers and readers.<br /><br />Charles de Lint writes like a magician. He draws out the strange inside our own world, weaving stories that feel more real than we are when we read them. He is, simply put, the best. <br />—Holly Black (bestselling author)<br />Charles de Lint is the modern master of urban fantasy. Folktale, myth, fairy tale, dreams, urban legend—all of it adds up to pure magic in de Lint's vivid, original world. No one does it better. <br />—Alice Hoffman (bestselling author)<br /><br />To read de Lint is to fall under the spell of a master storyteller, to be reminded of the greatness of life, of the beauty and majesty lurking in shadows and empty doorways. <br />—Quill &amp; Quire<br /><br />His Newford books, which make up most of de Lint's body of work between 1993 and 2009, confirmed his reputation for bringing a vivid setting and repertory cast of characters to life on the page. Though not a consecutive series, the twenty-five standalone books set in (or connected to) Newford give readers a feeling of visiting a favourite city and seeing old friends.<br />More recently, his young adult Wildlings trilogy—Under My Skin, Over My Head, and Out of This World—came out from Penguin Canada and Triskell Press in 2012, 2013 and 2014. Under My Skin won 2013 Aurora Award. A novel for middle-grade readers, The Cats of Tanglewood Forest, published by Little Brown in 2013, won the Sunburst Award, earned starred reviews in both Publishers Weekly and Quill &amp; Quire, and was chosen by the New York Times Editors as one of the top six children's books for 2013. His most recent adult novel, The Mystery of Grace (2009), is a fascinating ghost story about love, passion and faith. It was a finalist for both the Sunburst and Evergreen awards.<br /><br />De Lint is presently writing a new adult novel. His storytelling skills also shine in his original songs. He and MaryAnn (also a musician) recently released companion CDs of their original songs, samples of which can be heard on de Lint's website. A multi-instrumentalist, his main instruments are guitar, harmonica and vocals, while MaryAnn's are mandolin, guitar, vocals and percussion.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9923028872958170514">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/8185168.Charles_de_Lint" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Charles  de Lint...</a>

Mulengro, Angel of Darkness and From a Whisper to a Scream (the latter two first published under the pen name of Samuel M. Key) were all, at their heart, police procedurals, sparked mostly, I\'d guess, from years of reading Ed McBain. I\'d also touched on spy thrillers (the RCMP sections of Moonheart), tropes such as organized crime (the Mafia in Greenmantle), and various hardboiled characters who\'ve shown up in the pages of various novels and stories. \n\n&amp;quot;But this was the first time that I sat down to deliberately write a mystery novel, with a PI as a lead character, and no fantasy elements whatsoever, hedging my bets only slightly by giving Jevon &amp;quot;Jake&amp;quot; Swann a love for Celtic music. (It doesn\'t matter where you put Celtic music; it always holds a touch of magic to it.) And then I set the story in Ottawa, because that\'s where I was living at the time and I liked having my characters walk around in the same neighbourhoods that I did, or could.&amp;quot;\n--Charles de
